                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form>, (inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">تَفْرِيسٌ</foreign>, TA,) <hi rend="ital">He</hi> (a wild beast) <hi rend="ital">seized often the sheep</hi> or <hi rend="ital">goats,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">seized many of them, and broke,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">crushed so as to break, their necks.</hi> (M, TA.)       <sense type="A" n="2">-A2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">فرّسه الشَّىْءَ</foreign>, (inf. n. as above, TA,) <hi rend="ital">He exposed to him</hi> (namely a wild beast) <hi rend="ital">the thing,</hi> [meaning the animal,] <hi rend="ital">that he might seize it, and break,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">crush so as to break, its neck:</hi> and <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n33488-1" target="أَفْرَسَهُ" n="1" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>إَيَّاهُ</foreign>

                  <hi rend="ital">the man left his ass to the lion, that he might break his neck,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">kill him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">make him his prey, while he himself should escape.</hi> (S, K.)                      <L>

                     </L> 
                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">A beating which, when it falls upon the tops of heads, digs, in the pates, hollows that afford prey to the blue stinging flies</hi>]; meaning, that these wounds are wide, and enable the <foreign lang="ar">نعر</foreign> to obtain <pb n="2367"/> thence what they desire. (M.)                      </L>

                        <foreign lang="ar">أَتَتْهُ ذِئَابٌ لَا يُبَالِينَ رَاعِيًا</foreign>

                        <foreign lang="ar">وَكُنُّ سَوَامًا تَشْتَهِى أَنْ تُفَرَّسَا</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">They had sent me among the girls with swelling breasts, as a guardian; and, by my father, while guardian of the girls with swelling breasts,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">by the father of the guardian of the girls with swelling breasts, I was</hi> (lit. <hi rend="ital">I am</hi>) <hi rend="ital">made a prey: there came thither wolves not caring for a guardian, and those females were</hi> (as) <hi rend="ital">pasturing camels eagerly desiring to be given as prey</hi>]: he likens these women to pasturing camels, although differing from them inasmuch as the latter do not eagerly desire to be given as prey, since this would be a cause of their death, whereas women do eagerly desire it, since <foreign lang="ar">فَرْسُ الرِّجَالِ لِلنِّسَآءِ</foreign> [lit. <hi rend="ital">men's making women their prey</hi>] is in this case <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">men's holding commerce of love with women:</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">أُفْرَسُ</foreign> is for <foreign lang="ar">فُرِسْتُ</foreign>; for, as Sb says, they sometimes put <foreign lang="ar">أَفْعَلُ</foreign> in the place of <foreign lang="ar">فَعَلْتُ</foreign>: <foreign lang="ar">أَبِى</foreign> is in the gen. case as governed by <foreign lang="ar">وَ</foreign> denoting swearing; and <foreign lang="ar">راعى الكواعب</foreign> may be a denotative of state relating to the <foreign lang="ar">ت</foreign> [the pronoun of the first person] understood [in <foreign lang="ar">أُفْرَسُ</foreign> for <foreign lang="ar">فُرِسْتُ</foreign>]; or <foreign lang="ar">وأبى</foreign> may be prefixed to <foreign lang="ar">راعى الكواعب</foreign>, governing it in the gen. case, and by the latter expression he may mean himself: by wolves not caring for a guardian, he means wicked men not caring for him who guarded these women: and he uses the word <foreign lang="ar">تشتهى</foreign> to denote intense desire; for if he did not mean intenseness, he would have said <foreign lang="ar">تُرِيدُ</foreign>.
